## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillator. Common models in this domain specify dv_dt as a sum of restoring-force terms in x, damping terms in v, and external/parametric forcing terms in t (and sometimes x,v).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring acceleration)
- Linear damping oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (velocity-opposing constant-magnitude friction)
- Quadratic/drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent-like drag or nonlinear dissipation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strong nonlinearity at large amplitudes)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillator with amplitude-limited limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (negative damping at small v, positive at large v)
- Liénard-type oscillator (general nonlinear damping + restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (broad class including many limit-cycle systems)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x - c4 * v (Mathieu/Duffing-like parametric drive)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (canonical forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Conservative potential form: dv_dt = -D_xU where U = c0 * x**2 + c1 * x**4 + c2 * x**6 (acceleration from polynomial potential energy gradient)
- Non-smooth piecewise stiffness (impact/bistable approximation): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x - c2 * v (effective stiffness changes with amplitude/sign)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force structure: if the system is energy-conserving (no damping/forcing), dv_dt tends to be a function of x only and often an odd function of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - c*x^3).
- Viscous damping signature: dissipation that is linear in v produces dv_dt terms proportional to -v; higher-speed drag often appears as -v*Abs(v).
- Self-excitation / limit-cycle signature: terms like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, yielding stable oscillations.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: +x**3 in the restoring force magnitude (i.e., dv_dt includes -c*x - c*x^3 with c>0) typically hardens (frequency increases with amplitude); opposite sign softens.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t + phase) or cos(c*t + phase) terms suggest a driven oscillator; multiple harmonics may appear if forcing is non-sinusoidal.
- Parametric resonance indicator: time-multiplying stiffness or damping (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) suggests Mathieu-type behavior and resonance bands.
- Odd/even symmetry clues: purely elastic symmetric springs often yield dv_dt odd in x; asymmetry (even powers, Abs(x)) suggests unilateral constraints, pre-load, or non-symmetric potentials.
- Non-smooth dissipation clues: sign(v) or Abs(v) terms indicate dry friction, impacts, or piecewise contact laws rather than smooth viscous damping.
- State-coupling beyond additive forces: products like x*v or x**2*v often indicate geometry-dependent damping or Liénard-form transformations rather than simple linear damping.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO32)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
f(x,t,v)=0.56911073046847\sin t\;-\;0.0907042821530562\,v^3\;-\;0.594472842575296\,v\,e^{-|v|}\;-\;2.9429090494833\,x^3.
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Must contain **exactly** a \(\sin(t)\) term (can be written as cosine with phase shift), coefficient \(0.5691...\).
- Must contain **\(-2.9429...\,x^3\)** and **no other x-dependence**.
- Must contain **\(-0.090704...\,v^3\)**.
- Must contain the non-polynomial damping term **\(-0.59447...\, v e^{-|v|}\)**, which is **not representable** by any finite combination of pure powers of \(v\), logs, rational functions, or \(e^{c v}\) without \(|v|\). Also note the strict rule: \(|v|\) cannot be dropped since \(v\) can be negative.

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–18 (cos(t+const) + polynomial in v + x^3 + maybe constants/linear v)
All of 1–18 have only algebraic terms in \(v\): sums of \(v^{p}\) and \(v\) (and constants), plus \(x^3\), plus a cosine-in-time term.
- Time term: \(c0\cos(c1+t)\) can match \(0.5691\sin t\) by choosing \(c1=\pi/2\) and \(c0=-0.56911073046847\) (since \(\cos(t+\pi/2)=-\sin t\)). So time part is fine.
- \(x^3\): can match by setting the \(x^3\) coefficient to \(-2.9429090494833\).
- \(v^3\): can match by setting one exponent to 3 and coefficient to \(-0.0907042821530562\).
- **But** none of 1–18 contains \(v e^{-|v|}\) or any \(|v|\) or \(e^{-|v|}\) dependence. A finite polynomial in \(v\) cannot equal \(v e^{-|v|}\) for all real \(v\).
Therefore **1–18 cannot match**.

### Candidate 19
\(c0\cos(c1 t+c2)+ c3 v^{c4}+ c5 v^3+ c6 v^5+ c7 v+ c8 x^3\).
Same issue: only powers of \(v\), no \(v e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

### Candidates 20–21
Cosine time + \(v^3\) + \(v^{c4}\) + \(v^5\) + \(v\) + \(x^3\) (+ constant in 21).
Still no \(v e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 22
Adds a constant \(c6\), still only powers of \(v\). **No match**.

### Candidates 23, 31, 41, 44 (contain \(\sin(\text{linear in }v)\) or extra \(\sin(\text{linear in }t)\) or \(\sin(\text{linear in }x)\))
Example 23: \(c0\cos(c1+t)+ c2\sin(c3 v+c4)+ \dots\)
- GT has **no sinusoid in \(v\)** (or in \(x\), or extra in \(t\) besides \(\sin t\)).
- You could set \(c2=0\) to remove the \(\sin(\cdot)\) term, but then you’re back to polynomial-in-\(v\) only, still missing \(v e^{-|v|}\).
So **23, 31, 41, 44 cannot match**.

### Candidates 24–30 (cos(c1 t + c2) + polynomial powers including v^3/v^5 + linear v + x^3 + maybe v^{c7})
All are sums of monomials \(v^p\) (and possibly an extra \(v^{c7}\)), no \(|v|\) and no \(e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

### Candidates 32–36, 48, 50 (rational functions in v, plus v^3, plus cos time, plus x^3)
These include terms like \(v/(c6 v+c7)\) or \(c8/(c6 v+c7)\), etc.
- Rational functions still cannot reproduce \(v e^{-|v|}\) globally for all real \(v\).
- Also they introduce poles unless coefficients are set to remove them; setting them to 0 again leaves only polynomials, still missing the exponential-with-Abs term.
So **32–36, 48, 50 cannot match**.

### Candidate 34
Includes \(c6/(c7 v+c8)\) plus \(v^3\). Same rational-function issue; cannot equal \(v e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 37
Has \(c0\sqrt(c1+x^2)\cos(c2+t)\) which introduces \(\sqrt(c1+x^2)\) dependence; GT’s time forcing is independent of \(x\). Only way to remove is \(c0=0\), but then you lose the required \(\sin t\) term. So **cannot match** even before considering the damping term. **No match**.

### Candidate 38
Has \(c4\log(c5 v+1)\) plus polynomial terms.
- \(\log(1+c5 v)\) cannot equal \(v e^{-|v|}\) for all real \(v\).
- Also domain issues for log when \(1+c5 v\le 0\) unless \(c5=0\) (then log term becomes \(\log 1=0\)), which again removes it and leaves only polynomials.
So **no match**.

### Candidates 39–40, 47 (contain \(exp(c5 v)\) and log terms)
They include \(c4\exp(c5 v)\) (no absolute value) and logs.
- GT needs \(\exp(-|v|)\), which is **even** in \(v\) inside the exponential and is not representable by \(\exp(c5 v)\) for all real \(v\) (since \(\exp(c5 v)\) is not symmetric unless \(c5=0\), which makes it constant).
- Even allowing combinations, these candidates only have a single \(\exp(c5 v)\) term (not piecewise), and no \(|v|\). Cannot match globally.
So **39, 40, 47 no match**.

### Candidates 42–43 (time-dependent denominators)
Contain terms like \(v/(c7 t+c8)\) or \(x/(c7 t+c8)\) and \(1/(c7 t+c8)\).
- GT has no such rational-in-time terms. To remove them you’d set corresponding coefficients to 0, reverting to polynomial-in-\(v\) + \(v^3\) + \(x^3\) + cosine time, still missing \(v e^{-|v|}\).
So **no match**.

### Candidate 45
Has \(c4\exp(c5 t)\) (time exponential) which GT does not have. Setting \(c4=0\) removes it, but then again only polynomial in \(v\), missing \(v e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 46
Has rational functions in \(x\): \(x/(c5 x+c6)\) and \(1/(c5 x+c6)\), which GT does not have. Setting their coefficients to 0 removes them, again leaving no \(v e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 49
Has \(v/(c7 x+c8)\) and \(1/(c7 x+c8)\) coupling \(v\) with \(x\); GT has no such coupling. Removing them still leaves no \(v e^{-|v|}\). **No match**.

---

**Conclusion:** Every candidate lacks the essential non-polynomial, absolute-value exponential damping term \(-0.594472842575296\, v e^{-|v|}\). Since \(v\) takes negative values, there is no permissible domain restriction that would allow replacing \(|v|\) with \(v\) or otherwise eliminating the need for \(|v|\). Therefore none can be made exactly equivalent to the fixed GT by parameter choice.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO32)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0907*v³ - 0.5945*v*exp(-|v|) - 2.9429*x³ + 0.5691*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `sin(t)` — can be written as `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift
2. `v³` — polynomial in v
3. `v*exp(-|v|)` — this is a specific non-polynomial, non-rational function of v
4. `x³` — polynomial in x

The critical term is `v*exp(-|v|)`. This function cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials in v (like v, v³, v⁵)
- Rational functions of v
- `sin(v)` or `log(v+1)` terms
- Simple combinations of the above

Let me check each candidate systematically.

**Candidates 1-18, 20-21, 26:** These contain terms like `v^c_i` (power functions) and linear `v` terms, but no `exp(-|v|)` term. Power functions `v^c` cannot reproduce `v*exp(-|v|)` for all v. These are **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 19, 22, 24-25, 27-30:** These have `cos(c1*t + c2)` which requires `c1=1` for matching. They contain polynomial terms in v (v³, v⁵, v^c) but no `exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 23, 31:** Contains `sin(c3*v + c4)` — sin is periodic and bounded, while `v*exp(-|v|)` is not periodic. Cannot match. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 32-36, 48, 50:** Contains rational terms like `v/(c*v + c)`. Rational functions cannot equal `v*exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 37:** Has `sqrt(c1 + x²)*cos(c2 + t)` — this couples x and t, which GT doesn't have (unless c1=0, giving |x|*cos, still wrong). **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 38:** Contains `log(c5*v + 1)` — logarithmic, not exponential decay. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 39, 40, 47:** Contains `exp(c5*v)` and `log(c7*v + 1)`. The GT has `v*exp(-|v|)`. Note `exp(c5*v)` is `exp` of v (not |v|). For v > 0, `v*exp(-|v|) = v*exp(-v)`, and for v < 0, `v*exp(-|v|) = v*exp(v)`. A single `exp(c*v)` cannot capture both sides. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 41:** Has `sin(c3*t + c4)` as extra term — can be absorbed into the cos term only if frequencies match (both are frequency 1 in t). `c0*cos(c1+t) + c2*sin(c3*t+c4)` with c3=1 gives a single sinusoid in t. But still lacks `exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 42-43, 49:** Contains terms with t or x in denominators coupled with v. These introduce dependencies that GT doesn't have and can't be zeroed without losing needed terms. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 44:** Has `sin(c3*x + c4)` — sin of x cannot match x³ behavior. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 45:** Has `exp(c5*t)` — exponential in t, GT has no such term. Setting c4=0 removes it, but then no `exp(-|v|)` term remains. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 46:** Rational in x, not matching. **NO MATCH**.

None of the candidates contain `v*exp(-|v|)` or any equivalent representation. The function `v*exp(-|v|)` is a fundamentally distinct basis function that cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, trigonometric functions, or simple exponentials of v.
